            "description": "\nConcentriq stores files for some resource types. We expose an [AWS S3 Compatible API](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_S3) to our **Files Service** where you can directly interact with files for specific resources. With this Files API, you can get credentials to upload and download files in the Files service.\n\n## Storage Keys\n\nA resource may have one or more `storageKey`s which is the location of a specific file in the File Service. To use this API you will need this key, the `resourceType` and `resourceId` of the resource which contains it.\n\n## Uploading\n\nTo upload a file, you can use the `getUploadCredentials` endpoint to generate a scoped, temporary set of credentials to make upload requests to the Files Service. Once the file has been uploaded, you need to make a call to the `completeUpload` endpoint so Concentriq knows that it is ready to be used.\n\nIf STS is not available, you'll need to create a MultipartUpload and get signed urls from the API.\n\t1. Call  `createMultiPartUpload` and to start a MultipartUpload\n\t2. For each part, get a signed url with `getSignedMultiPartUploadUrl` and make a PUT request to that URL with the body and signed headers\n\t3. Call `completeMultiPartUpload` to complete the upload to S3\n\t5. Once the file has been uploaded, you need to make a call to the `completeUpload` endpoint so Concentriq knows that it is ready to be used.\n\n## Downloading\n\nTo download a file, you can make a call to the `getDownloadRedirect` endpoint. This returns an HTTP redirect to the target file in the File Service.\n"

        {
            "name": "CaseDetails",
            "description": "A CaseDetail is a representation of a Case. The nomenclature \"CaseDetail\" was chosen because \"Case\" in many programming languages is a reserved word. The CaseDetail is the encompassing object for all the given resources associated with a case. \n\n## Relations \n\n### User \n\nA CaseDetail is associated with the User object through the `createdBy` property, which is the id of the User.\n\n### AssignedUser\n\nA CaseDetail can only be associated with one User object through the `assignedUserId` property. \n\n### LabSite\n\nA CaseDetail can only be associated with one LabSite object through the `labSiteId` property. \n\n### Slides\n\nA CaseDetail can have many Slide objects related to it. Each Slide has a `caseDetailId` property to relate it to a CaseDetail. \n\n### CaseParts \n\nA CaseDetail can be associated to many CaseParts. A CasePart must only be associated with one CaseDetail. Each CasePart has a `caseDetailId` property to relate it to a CaseDetail.\n\n### CaseTags\n\nA CaseDetail can have many CaseTags related to it. A CaseTag can belong to multiple CaseDetails. The CaseDetailCaseTag object manages the relationship between CaseDetails and CaseTags.\n\n### CaseDetailCaseTag \n\nA CaseDetailCaseTag can only be associated with one caseDetail. A CaseDetail can have multiple CaseDetailCaseTags. The `caseDetailId` property is the id of the CaseDetail referenced by the CaseDetailCaseTag.\n\n### FirstReadAnalysis\n\nA CaseDetail can be associated with one FirstReadAnalysis. If so, the most recent FirstReadAnalysis is associated with the CaseDetail. A FirstReadAnalysis must be associated with one of the following: CaseDetail, Slide, or CasePart. Each FirstReadAnalysis has a `caseDetailId` property to relate it to a CaseDetail. \n"
        },
        {
            "name": "CaseParts",
            "description": "A CasePart is a representation of a physical tissue sample that is under study and includes all associated metadata with the sample. \n\n## Relations\n\n### CaseDetail\n\nA CasePart must be associated with one CaseDetail object. There can be many CaseParts per one CaseDetail. The `caseDetailId` property is the id of the CaseDetail referenced by the CasePart.\n\n### FirstReadAnalysis\n\nA CasePart can be associated with one FirstReadAnalysis. If so, the most recent FirstReadAnalysis is associated with the CasePart. A FirstReadAnalysis must be associated with one of the following: CaseDetail, Slide, or CasePart. Each FirstReadAnalysis has a `casePartId` property to relate it to a CaseDetail. \n\n### Procedure\nA CasePart can be associated with one Procedure. There can be many CaseParts per one Procedure. The `procedureId` property of the CasePart references the id of a Procedure.\n\n### Specimen\nA CasePart can be associated with one Specimen. There can be many CaseParts per one Specimen. The `specimenId` property of the CasePart references the id of a Specimen."

            "name": "FirstReadAnalyses",
            "description": "A FirstReadAnalysis represents an invocation of a FirstReadAnalysisApp on a CaseDetail and/or its descendants. It maintains the status of an ongoing analysis and its eventual success or failure. A FirstReadAnalysis can be associated with only one of either CaseDetail, CasePart, or Slide, but each FirstReadAnalysis can be referenced by its `parentAnalysisId` representing the case object hierarchy. Typically, a case's FirstReadAnalysis is an aggregation of the results of its child analyses. \n\n## Relations\n\n### CaseDetail \n\nA FirstReadAnalysis can only be associated to one CaseDetail object. There can only be one FirstReadAnalysis per CaseDetail. The `caseDetailId` property is the id of the CaseDetail referenced by the FirstReadAnalysis. \n### CasePart\n\nA FirstReadAnalysis can only be associated to one CasePart object. There can only be one FirstReadAnalysis per CasePart. The `casePartId` property is the id of the CasePart referenced by the FirstReadAnalysis. \n\n### FirstReadAnalysisApp\n\nA FirstReadAnalysisApp is the application that defines the FirstReadAnalysis. The `firstReadAnalysisAppId` property is the id of the FirstReadAnalysisApp referenced by the FirstReadAnalysis. \n\n### FirstReadAnalysisParent\n\nA FirstReadAnalysisParent is the parent FirstReadAnalysis of a FirstReadAnalysis. The `parentAnalysisId` property is the id of the FirstReadAnalysisParent referenced by the FirstReadAnalysis. \n\n### Slide\n\nA FirstReadAnalysis can only be associated to one Slide object. There can only be one FirstReadAnalysis per Slide. The `slideId` property is the id of the Slide referenced by the FirstReadAnalysis. \n"

            "name": "UserDefinedFields",
            "description": "UDFs are arbitrary fields defined by users for a variety of object types. Every UDF has three main components: key, resource type, and json schema. The json schema is where the type is defined. \n\n\n### Creating a UDF\n\nFirst use the create UDF api key below to initialize the UDF for a particular resource type. Then to actually create an object that has your UDF(s), follow that API's create method and be sure to include the key and desired value for the UDF you want to input in the \"udf\" property. Just because a UDF is created for an object, does not mean that it will initialize automatically.\n\n### Validation\n\nWhen assigning a UDF in a post request for an object, be sure to have the following:\n  - the key must exist in the object's possible User Defined Fields.\n  - the value's type must be consistent with the type that was defined in the UDF's jsonSchema.\n\n### Updating a UDF's value\n\nWhen updating a UDF's value, refer to the object's patch request in this API documentation. It is important to note that patches don't overwrite fields that aren't referenced. There will not be a full overwrite of the udf object. It will only update the udf values that you specify. \n\n\nSee the section on \"Filtering with object fields\" to learn about querying for them."

            "name": "UserRoles",
            "description": "UserRoles are a set of permissions granted to a user in the system. Each User must have exactly one UserRole. UserRoles may be deactivated by setting the `deactivated` property to true, as long as there are no users currently assigned to that role. \n\nThe permissions are generally in one of four categories:\n\t1. What resources a user can access, or read. \n\t2. What a user can do with resources they have access to (update, delete).\n\t3. What resources a user can create.\n\t4. What screens a user can access in the UI.\n\nThe primary access model of Concentriq is focused on the CaseDetail. A user can access a case if they are assigned to that case, or if the case is assigned to a LabSite that the user is a member of. If the role `canAccessAllCases`, then the user can access any case in the application.\n\n## Fields \n\nMost of the UserRole fields describe permissions with either boolean or enum values. Boolean fields indicate whether a user can or cannot perform a certain action (e.g., read API docs). Enum fields define more granular permissions. The enums are generally standardized as:\n\n- `full` - ability to create, read, update, and delete resource\n- `modify` - ability to create, read, and update resource\n- `readOnly` - ability to read resource \n- `none` - cannot read or perform any other action on resource\n\nSeveral fields have unique enum options, which are described in the specific field's documentation.\n\n## Relations\n\nA UserRole can be associated with one or more User objects. A User will only be associated with one UserRole through the User's `roleId` property.\n"

        {
            "name": "Webhooks",
            "description": "Webhooks enable your application to be notified by Concentriq when specified events occur. For example, use webhooks to receive a notification from Concentriq when an Image is created so that your application can take some action related to the new Image.\n\nThere are two steps to setting up a webhook.\n1. Expose a webhook endpoint on your application server with code to handle the webhook requests.\n2. Create a Webhook object via the Concentriq API that specifies your webhook endpoint and which events to send notifications for.\n\nWhen the second step is completed, Concentriq will begin sending HTTP POST requests to your webhook endpoint when the specified events occur.\n\n## Creating a Webhook Endpoint\n\nAdd a POST handler to your application server for your desired webhook endpoint. The handler should return an HTTP success or failure code quickly (i.e., without executing lengthy asynchronous work) in order to inform the Concentriq API whether the webhook request was successful.\n\n## Registering a Webhook with Concentriq\n\nConcentriq's `Create Webhook` API endpoint will add a Webhook object to the Concentriq database. This object is referenced to determine when an event should prompt a webhook notifcation. The API can also be used to view, update, and delete Webhook objects.\n\nThe Webhook includes the URL of your application's webhook handler, as well as the resource and event types that trigger the webhook (like Image creation). Filters and watched properties may also be applied to further constrain the list of qualifying events.\n\nA signing secret must also be included. This will be used to sign webhook request headers that verify the webhook request sender.\n\n## Signing with Headers\n\nWhen creating a webhook, generate and provide the signing secret that will be used to generate a hash key signature. The signature is a SHA-256 HMAC encoding of the webhook request's timestamp and request body signed with the signingSecret. The signature payload takes the form `<timestamp>.<JSON request body>` -- note the `.` delimiter.\n\nMake the signing secret available to your application. When your application receives webhook requests, decode the signature to verify that the request was sent by Concentriq. \n\n1. Read the `webhook-signature` and `webhook-timestamp` headers from the request. \n2. Read the JSON request body.\n3. Concatenate the signature payload `<timestamp>.<JSON request body>`\n4. Generate your own HMAC encoding of the signature payload with the SHA-256 hash function, using the signing secret as the key.\n5. Compare the received and computed signatures. If the two match, then the received signature is valid.\n\nAs an example, steps 3 and 4 can be accomplished in Node using the following function.\n\n```js\nimport Crypto from 'crypto';\n\nfunction getSignature (timestamp, body, signingSecret) {\n\tconst dataString = JSON.stringify(body);\n\tconst payload = `${timestamp}.${dataString}`;\n\treturn Crypto.createHmac('sha256', signingSecret).update(payload, 'utf8').digest('hex');\n}\n```\n\nThe returned string can then be compared to the signature received in the `webhook-signature` header.\n\n## Webhook Requests\n\nWebhook requests are POST requests from the Concentriq API to the webhook endpoint you've provided. Each request is made over HTTP and the results are written to the database as a WebhookRequest. If an attempt is unsuccessful, the WebhookRequest is re-queued and retried several times over several seconds until successful or a limit is reached. \n\nPast WebhookRequest attempts, both successful and unsuccessful can be viewed via the API. See the `WebhookRequests` endpoint documentation.\n\n## Best Practices\n\n- Do not listen for more events than are needed for your integration. Doing so will direct unnecessary webhook request traffic to your server. Consider disabling unused webhooks via the `Update Webhook` endpoint.\n\n- Webhook requests may not necessarily reach your server in the order in which the events occured. As such, your application logic should not rely on the order of events. \n\n- Verify header signatures as described above in order to confirm that webhook requests were sent by Concentriq and keep your application secure.\n\n- If you believe your signing signature has been exposed or is no longer secret for any reason, roll the signing secret as quickly as possible using the `Update Webhook` endpoint. Make sure that your application then uses the new secret when verifying received webhook requests.\n\n- Use an HTTPS URL for your webhook endpoint whenever possible.\n"
        },

        {
            "name": "Filters and Pagination",
            "x-traitTag": true,
            "description": "Many resources support endpoints which return a subset of all resources for a particular `resourceType`. They respond with the `items` as an array of the type queried and a `total` which is the total number of resources which match on your query. The results are always restricted to the resources you have access to.\n\n## Filters\n\nThe `filter` parameter on these endpoints allow you to query for specific resources. With the `eager` parameter you can build a query to limit items that match the values provided, values of related resources, and aggregations of related resources.\n\n### Filtering the base resource\n\nYou can filter the base resource by adding a `$where` clause at the root at the `eager` expression. The query language is a subset of the [MongoDB Query Language](https://docs.mongodb.com/manual/tutorial/query-documents/) which lets you use logical operators to build expressive queries.\n\nThis filter will return only fluorescence Images between 10,000 and 5000 pixels wide. \n`GET /api/v2/images`\n```json\n{\n\t\"eager\": {\n\t\t\"$where\": {\n\t\t\t\"illumination\": \"fluorescence\",\n\t\t\t\"$and\": [\n\t\t\t\t{\n\t\t\t\t\t\"width\": { \"$lte\": 10000 }\n\t\t\t\t},\n\t\t\t\t{\n\t\t\t\t\t\"width\": { \"$gte\": 5000 }\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t]\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Filtering and adding relations\n\nMany resources have relationships which can be rendered in the output or used in queries. \n\nYou can simply add the related resources by using a boolean. To get all images for a slide:\n`GET /api/v2/slides`\n\n```json\n{\n\t\"eager\": {\n\t\t\"image\": true\n\t}\n}\n```\n\nYou can filter the base resource without returning relations by addressing them in the base `$where` clause:\n`GET /api/v2/slides`\n\n```json\n{\n\t\"eager\": {\n\t\t\"$where\": {\n\t\t\t\"image.illumination\": \"fluorescence\"\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n```\n\nYou can also filter the related output individually by using `$where` on their subqueries. This query will return all slides but only return fluorescent images:\n`GET /api/v2/slides`\n\n```json\n{\n\t\"eager\": {\n\t\t\"image\": {\n\t\t\t\"$where\": {\n\t\t\t\t\"illumination\": \"fluorescence\"\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\t\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Filtering with object fields\n\nSome resources have object fields which the query builder does not interpret as relations. One such field is the `udf` field on resources that support UDFs. These fields can be addressed with a special syntax, using `$` instead of a dot operator, to let the query know that you are referring to the object instead of a relationship.\n\n```json\n{\n\t\"eager\": {\n\t\t\"$where\": {\n\t\t\t\"udf$numberField\": 123\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Aggregations\n\n`$aggregations` let you run various functions across the set of all items and their relationships. You can use the output of these aggregations in the query itself or in the items returned by the query.\n\nThis query will only return slides that have annotations. `numAnnotations` will also appear in each item of the array.\n\n`GET /api/v2/slides`\n```json\n{\n\t\"eager\": {\n\t\t\"$aggregations\": [\n\t\t\t{\n\t\t\t\t\"type\": \"count\",\n\t\t\t\t\"alias\": \"numAnnotations\",\n\t\t\t\t\"relation\": \"annotations\"\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t],\n\t\t\"$where\": {\n\t\t\t\"numAnnotations\": { \"$gte\": 1 }\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n## Pagination\n\nIt is advisable to limit the results of an API call so you don't overwhelm your application. You can use the `filter` parameter to specify a `limit` which specifies how many rows to fetch at once. You can also use `offset` as a cursor to make several calls which return the entire set based on the `limit`.\nSince each respons returns an array, you can also specify an `order` expression to sort the entire set.\n\n### Fields\n\nUsing the `fields` expression lets you limit which properties that should be in each item of the response.\n"
        }
